## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which most naturally corresponds to constitutive laws for solids (elasticity/plasticity/viscoelasticity) with temperature-dependent stiffness, thermal strain, and temperature-driven softening or strengthening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic (Hooke + thermal strain): sigma = E(T) * (epsilon - alpha(T) * (T - c0)) (small-strain solids with thermal expansion)
- Hooke’s law with linear temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness changes approximately linearly over a limited T range)
- Hooke’s law with polynomial modulus in temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (empirical E(T) fits over wider temperature ranges)
- Thermal-stress-only (fully constrained body): sigma = c0 * alpha(T) * (T - c1) (stress generated when thermal strain is prevented)
- Bilinear elastic–plastic with temperature-dependent yield: sigma = Min((c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon, sigma_y(T) + H(T) * (epsilon - epsilon_y(T))) (simple plasticity with T-softening/strengthening)
- Ramberg–Osgood with temperature dependence: epsilon = sigma / E(T) + c0 * (sigma / sigma0(T))**c1 (nonlinear elastic/plastic transition with T-dependent parameters)
- Power-law hardening with T-dependent strength coefficient: sigma = K(T) * (c0 + epsilon)**n(T) (empirical plastic flow curve; offsets avoid singularity at epsilon=0)
- Exponential temperature softening of strength: sigma = g(epsilon) * exp(-c0 * T) (thermally activated softening captured phenomenologically)
- Sigmoidal temperature softening of modulus/strength: sigma = g(epsilon) / (1 + c0 * exp(c1 * T)) (smooth transition across a softening regime, e.g., near glass transition)
- Piecewise elastic-to-nonlinear elastic (strain stiffening/softening): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**3 (Landau-style or polynomial nonlinearity at larger strains)
- Exponential strain-stiffening with temperature-dependent scale: sigma = A(T) * (exp(c0 * epsilon) - 1) (common for polymers/rubbers under finite strain, used as a fit form)
- Multiplicative separability (common regression ansatz): sigma = f(epsilon) * h(T) (when temperature primarily scales the stress level without changing curve shape)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: sigma ∝ epsilon at small epsilon suggests Hookean behavior; deviations indicate plasticity or nonlinear elasticity.
- Temperature-dependent stiffness: if d(sigma)/d(epsilon) decreases with increasing T at fixed epsilon, model E(T) as a decreasing function (linear/polynomial or exp(-c*T)).
- Thermal expansion offset: if sigma at epsilon≈0 shifts with T, include an additive strain shift epsilon - alpha*(T-c0) (signature of thermal strain).
- Yield/flow stress reduction with T: if stress curves collapse after dividing by a T-dependent scale, use multiplicative separability sigma = f(epsilon)*h(T).
- Curve-shape change with T: if hardening exponent changes with T (e.g., more/less curvature), allow n(T) or nonlinear terms whose coefficients depend on T.
- Smooth transition across a characteristic temperature: if behavior changes rapidly near some T0, use logistic/sigmoidal dependence in T for E(T) or strength parameters.
- Avoid nonphysical negative stiffness: enforce E(T) > 0 by modeling E(T) as exp(p(T)) or (c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2) with constrained coefficients.
- Stress symmetry under strain sign: if data are tension-only, asymmetric models are fine; if both tension/compression exist, consider odd/even structure in epsilon (e.g., linear + cubic).

GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci9)
============================================================
GT: c0*epsilon**c1 - c2*(T - c3) + epsilon**c4*c5*(T - c6)
Candidate formulas: 61

GT (with fixed constants) can be rewritten as a polynomial in \(T\) with coefficients depending on \(\epsilon\):
\[
4.2558304788\,\epsilon^3\;-\;0.3902956878\,(T-308.8646781)\;+\;8.6380281543\,\epsilon^3\,(T-308.8646781).
\]
Expand:
\[
= \underbrace{\big(8.6380281543\,\epsilon^3 - 0.3902956878\big)}_{\text{coefficient of }T}\,T
\;+\;\underbrace{\Big(4.2558304788\,\epsilon^3 + (0.3902956878-8.6380281543\,\epsilon^3)\,308.8646781\Big)}_{\text{constant in }T}.
\]
So GT has:
- a \(T\epsilon^3\) term,
- a \(T\) term independent of \(\epsilon\),
- an \(\epsilon^3\) term independent of \(T\),
- and a pure constant term,
and **no** \(T\epsilon\), \(\epsilon\), trig/exp/log, \(|\epsilon|\), \(\epsilon^4\), \(1/T\), etc.

Now check candidates (constants in candidates are free; we may also impose a plausible domain condition like \(\epsilon\ge 0\) to drop Abs).

1) Has \(T\epsilon\), \((c3+|\epsilon|)^2\), cosine term. To match GT we’d need to kill all non-GT structures: set those coefficients to 0. Then remaining is at best \(T*c1*\epsilon^3 + c5\) (plus maybe \(c4\epsilon\) if not killed). Cannot create the required standalone \(T\) term and standalone \(\epsilon^3\) term simultaneously. No.

2) Rational function with denominator \(c1|\epsilon|^4+1\). To equal a polynomial in \(\epsilon\) for a continuous domain, must effectively make denominator constant: set \(c1=0\). Then expression becomes
\(T*c0\epsilon^3 + T*c2\epsilon^3|\epsilon|^4 + c3|\epsilon|^4 + c4\epsilon|\epsilon|^4 + c5\epsilon^3|\epsilon|^4 + c6\epsilon + c7 + c8\epsilon^3 + c9\epsilon\).
To match GT we must also set coefficients of \(|\epsilon|^4\), \(\epsilon|\epsilon|^4\), \(\epsilon\) to 0, leaving \(T*c0\epsilon^3 + c7 + c8\epsilon^3\). Still missing the required pure \(T\) term. No.

`T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c2*(c3 + |epsilon|)**2 + c4*epsilon + c5 + c6*(c3 + |epsilon|)**2 + c7*epsilon*exp(c8/T)`

Same (c3+|epsilon|)**2 issue. exp(c8/T) is not polynomial in T.

Candidate 19 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 20:
`T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c2 + T*c3*(c4 + |epsilon|)**2 + c5*|epsilon| + c6 + c7*epsilon + c8*(c4 + |epsilon|)**2`

This has T*c2 (standalone T term!). Let me check if we can zero out unwanted terms.

With epsilon ≥ 0: |epsilon| = epsilon.

Set c4=0: `(c4+epsilon)**2 = epsilon**2`
Then: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c2 + T*c3*epsilon**2 + c5*epsilon + c6 + c7*epsilon + c8*epsilon**2`

Basis: {T*epsilon, T*epsilon**3, T, T*epsilon**2, epsilon, 1, epsilon**2}

Need to zero out T*epsilon (set c0=0), T*epsilon**2 (set c3=0), epsilon (set c5+c7=0), epsilon**2 (set c8=0).

If c3=0, we lose T*epsilon**2 ✓. But then `c8*(c4+epsilon)**2` with c4=0 gives c8*epsilon**2. Set c8=0.

Remaining: `T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c2 + c6`

But we also need epsilon**3 term! We don't have a standalone epsilon**3 term.

Wait, let me re-examine. With c4=0, c0=0, c3=0:
`T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c2 + c5*epsilon + c6 + c7*epsilon + c8*epsilon**2`

Set c8=0, c5+c7=0: `T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c2 + c6`

Missing epsilon**3 term! 

What if c4≠0? Then (c4+epsilon)**2 = c4**2 + 2*c4*epsilon + epsilon**2.
T*c3*(c4+epsilon)**2 = T*c3*c4**2 + T*c3*2*c4*epsilon + T*c3*epsilon**2
c8*(c4+epsilon)**2 = c8*c4**2 + 2*c8*c4*epsilon + c8*epsilon**2

Full expression:
T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c2 + T*c3*c4**2 + T*c3*2*c4*epsilon + T*c3*epsilon**2 + c5*epsilon + c6 + c7*epsilon + c8*c4**2 + 2*c8*c4*epsilon + c8*epsilon**2

Basis: {T*epsilon, T*epsilon**3, T, T*epsilon**2, epsilon, 1, epsilon**2}

Still no standalone epsilon**3 term. Can't match GT.

Candidate 20 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 21:
`T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c2*(c3 + |epsilon|)**2 + T*c4 + c5 + c6*epsilon + c7*(c3 + |epsilon|)**2`

Has T*c4 (standalone T)! With epsilon ≥ 0:

Expand (c3+epsilon)**2 = c3**2 + 2*c3*epsilon + epsilon**2:
T*c2*(c3+epsilon)**2 = T*c2*c3**2 + T*2*c2*c3*epsilon + T*c2*epsilon**2
c7*(c3+epsilon)**2 = c7*c3**2 + 2*c7*c3*epsilon + c7*epsilon**2

Still no standalone epsilon**3! Can't match GT.

### Candidate 23:
`T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**c2 + T*c3*(c4 + |epsilon|)**c5 + c6*epsilon + c7 + c8*(c4 + |epsilon|)**c5`

With epsilon ≥ 0. Set c2=3: T*c1*epsilon**3.
Set c5=0: (c4+epsilon)**0 = 1. Then T*c3*1 = T*c3 and c8*1 = c8.

Full: T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c3 + c6*epsilon + c7 + c8

Set c0=0: `T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c3 + c6*epsilon + (c7+c8)`

Basis: {T*epsilon**3, T, epsilon, 1} - but missing epsilon**3!

What if c5=3, c4=0? Then (epsilon)**3.
T*c3*epsilon**3 + c8*epsilon**3. But then T*c1*epsilon**c2 needs to provide something else.

Actually with c4=0, c5=3:
T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**c2 + T*c3*epsilon**3 + c6*epsilon + c7 + c8*epsilon**3

If c2=3: T*(c1+c3)*epsilon**3 - only one T*epsilon**3 coefficient. Still missing standalone T.

What if c5=0 and c2=3?
T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c3 + c6*epsilon + c7 + c8
= T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c3 + c6*epsilon + const (set c0=0)

Missing epsilon**3. 

Hmm, what about c4≠0, c5=3?
(c4+epsilon)**3 = c4**3 + 3*c4**2*epsilon + 3*c4*epsilon**2 + epsilon**3

This introduces epsilon**2 terms that can't be zeroed independently.

Unless... we use both terms creatively. Let me think more carefully.

We need: T*b1*epsilon**3 + b2*T + b3*epsilon**3 + b4

From the candidate: T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**c2 + T*c3*(c4+epsilon)**c5 + c6*epsilon + c7 + c8*(c4+epsilon)**c5

Set c0=0, c6=0. Set c2=3: T*c1*epsilon**3.
Set c5=0: T*c3 + c8. Then: T*c1*epsilon**3 + T*c3 + c7 + c8.
Missing epsilon**3.

Alternative: set c5=3, c4=0: T*c3*epsilon**3 + c8*epsilon**3. Set c2 to something else to get T.
But c2 must be a power of epsilon, and T*c1*epsilon**c2 can't give standalone T (would need c2=0, giving T*c1, but then no epsilon**3 from this term).

Set c2=0: T*c1 (standalone T!). c5=3, c4=0: T*c3*epsilon**3 + c8*epsilon**3.
Full: T*c1 + T*c3*epsilon**3 + c8*epsilon**3 + c7

Basis: {T, T*epsilon**3, epsilon**3, 1} ✓ This matches!

Let me verify: c0=0, c6=0, c2=0, c4=0, c5=3.
`T*c1 + T*c3*epsilon**3 + c7 + c8*epsilon**3`

This has exactly the 4 basis functions we need!

Candidate 23 verdict: [MATCH]

= T*c0*epsilon**3 + (c1+c6)*epsilon + (c2+c4) + c5*epsilon**3
Missing T.

Can't get standalone T from exp(c3/T) for any c3≠0 (it's exponential, not linear).
